    "The purpose of this notebook is to extract all data pertaining to cookie storage and local Storage.\n",

   "source": [
    "### Cookie Data Extraction\n",
    "\n",
    "Cookie data is stored as a string in a key value scheme, example: \"splash_i = false; Adshow = 1;\".\n",
    "To extract and examine the data the script reduces it search to function calls with a symbol of: \"window.document.cookie\".\n",
    "The function then extracts the keys and values and stores it by the url of the script the function was called from."
   ]
  },

   "source": [
    "from urllib.parse import urlparse\n",
    "\n",
    "\n",
    "def extract_domain_name(data):\n",
    "  parsed_uri = urlparse( data )\n",
    "  return '{uri.scheme}://{uri.netloc}/'.format(uri=parsed_uri)\n",
    "\n",
    "\n",
    "result_cookie = result.loc[(result['symbol'] == \"window.document.cookie\") & (result['value'].str.contains(\"=\"))]\n",
    "cookiedf = pd.DataFrame(columns=['key', 'value', 'script_url'])\n",
    "for i, row in result_cookie.iterrows():\n",
    "    for kv in row['value'].split(\";\"):\n",
    "        if \"=\" in kv:\n",
    "            keyValueArr = kv.strip().split(\"=\", maxsplit=1)\n",
    "            cookiedf = cookiedf.append({'key':keyValueArr[0], 'value':keyValueArr[1], 'script_url':row['script_url'], 'location':extract_domain_name(row['location']), 'call_stack':row['call_stack']}, ignore_index=True) \n",
    "\n",
    "cookiedf\n",
    "\n"
   ]
  },

   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Cookie info\n",
    "\n",
    "The goal of this script is to search the cookiepedia api to see if their is any public information on the cookie key name. To prevent the script from flooding the cookiepedia API we cache the information returned by cookiepedia using a mini caching script: `from utils.simple_cache import Cache`\n",
    "\n",
    "[Cookiepedia](https://cookiepedia.co.uk/) is a public website with a database of cookie related information. We use their api to pull information on keys in the dataset"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 6,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "import requests\n",
    "from bs4 import BeautifulSoup\n",
    "import sys\n",
    "import urllib\n",
    "sys.path.append('..')\n",
    "from utils.simple_cache import Simple_Json_Cache\n",
    "\n",
    "\n",
    "def get_cookiepedia_data_by_cookie_key(key): \n",
    "    \"\"\" returns cookiepedia data or empty string, track empty strings as they are none requests not to make \"\"\"\n",
    "    url = 'https://cookiepedia.co.uk/cookies/' + urllib.parse.quote(key)\n",
    "    page = requests.get(url)\n",
    "    if page.status_code == 200:\n",
    "        soup = BeautifulSoup(page.content, 'html.parser')\n",
    "        node = soup.find(id=\"content-left\")\n",
    "        if node != None:\n",
    "            text = node.find('p').get_text()\n",
    "            if text:\n",
    "                return text\n",
    "    return \"\"\n",
    "\n",
    "cache = Simple_Json_Cache(\"cookiepedia\")\n",
    "\n",
    "for key in cookieKey.groups.keys():\n",
    "    cache_value = cache.get_value(key)\n",
    "    if not cache_value or cache_value != \"\": # we assume if cookie value == \"\" then we have checked cookiepedia and it has no data on the key\n",
    "        text = get_cookiepedia_data_by_cookie_key(key)\n",
    "        cache.set_value(key, text)\n",
    "\n",
    "                    \n",
    "cache.dump()\n"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Display all information found by cookiepedia"
   ]

     "text": [
      "_#env: This cookie name is associated with the tracking and attribution product from DC Storm, a UK subsidiary of Rakuten Marketing. The product helps site owners to link website visitor activity to external online marketing campaigns. This cookie supports collection of information about the users device, like screen size and browser.\n",
      "\n",
      "_gat: This cookie name is associated with Google Universal Analytics, according to documentation it is used to throttle the request rate - limiting the collection of data on high traffic sites. It expires after 10 minutes.\n",
      "\n",
      "_gid: This cookie name is asssociated with Google Universal Analytics. This appears to be a new cookie and as of Spring 2017 no information is available from Google.  It appears to store and update a unique value for each page visited.\n",
      "\n",
      "__gads: This cookie is associated with the DoubleClick for Publishers service from Google. Its purpose is to do with the showing of adverts on the site, for which the owner may earn some revenue.\n",
      "\n",
      "__atuvs: This cookie is associated with the AddThis social sharing widget which is commonly embedded in websites to enable visitors to share content with a range of networking and sharing platforms. This is believed to be a new cookie from AddThis which is not yet documented, but has been categorised on the assumption it serves a similar purpose to other cookies set by the service.\n",
      "\n",
      "_#srchist: This cookie name is associated with the tracking and attribution product from DC Storm, a UK subsidiary of Rakuten Marketing. The product helps site owners to link website visitor activity to external online marketing campaigns. This cookie stores the history of traffic sources the user has arrived to the site by.\n",
      "\n",
      "__utmb: This is one of the four main cookies set by the Google Analytics service which enables website owners to track visitor behaviour and measure site performance. This cookie determines new sessions and visits and expires after 30 minutes. The cookie is updated every time data is sent to Google Analytics. Any activity by a user within the 30 minute life span will count as a single visit, even if the user leaves and then returns to the site. A return after 30 minutes will count as a new visit, but a returning visitor.\n",
      "\n",
      "__utma: This is one of the four main cookies set by the Google Analytics service which enables website owners to track visitor behaviour and measure site performance. This cookie lasts for 2 years by default and distinguishes between users and sessions. It it used to calculate new and returning visitor statistics. The cookie is updated every time data is sent to Google Analytics. The lifespan of the cookie can be customised by website owners.\n",
      "\n",
      "_#uid: This cookie name is associated with the tracking and attribution product from DC Storm, a UK subsidiary of Rakuten Marketing. The product helps site owners to link website visitor activity to external online marketing campaigns. This cookie is a unique user identifier.\n",
      "\n",
      "_#tsa: This cookie name is associated with the tracking and attribution product from DC Storm, a UK subsidiary of Rakuten Marketing. The product helps site owners to link website visitor activity to external online marketing campaigns. This cookie stores referrer details to avoid duplicate counting of landing events.\n",
      "\n",
      "__utmv: This is an optional addtional cookie set by the Google Analytics service which enables website owners to track visitor behaviour and measure site performance. This cookie is used when site owners create custom visitor-level variables for customising what can be measured. The cookie is updated every time data is sent to Google Analytics. It has a default lifespan of two years, although this can be customised by site owners.\n",
      "\n",
      "__atuvc: This cookie  is associated with the AddThis social sharing widget which is commonly embedded in websites to enable visitors to share content with a range of networking and sharing platforms. It stores an updated page share count.\n",
      "\n",
      "__utmt: This cookie is set by Google Analytics.  According to their documentation it is used to throttle the request rate for the service - limiting the collection of data on high traffic sites. It expires after 10 minutes\n",
      "\n",
      "__utmc: This is one of the four main cookies set by the Google Analytics service which enables website owners to track visitor behaviour and measure site performance. It is not used in most sites but is set to enable interoperability with the older version of Google Analytics code known as Urchin.  In this older versions this was used in combination with the __utmb cookie to identify new sessions/visits for returning visitors.\n",
      "When used by Google Analytics this is always a Session cookie which is destroyed when the user closes their browser. Where it is seen as a Persistent cookie it is therefore likely to be a different technology setting the cookie.\n",
      "\n",
      "_#vdf: This cookie name is associated with the tracking and attribution product from DC Storm, a UK subsidiary of Rakuten Marketing. The product helps site owners to link website visitor activity to external online marketing campaigns. This cookie stores visit definition information.\n",
      "\n",
      "_#sess: This cookie name is associated with the tracking and attribution product from DC Storm, a UK subsidiary of Rakuten Marketing. The product helps site owners to link website visitor activity to external online marketing campaigns. This cookie reportedly stores information about a user session, although it is itself persistent.\n",
      "\n",
      "_ga: This cookie name is asssociated with Google Universal Analytics - which is a significant update to Google's more commonly used analytics service. This cookie is used to distinguish unique users by assigning a randomly generated number as a client identifier. It is included in each page request in a site and used to calculate visitor, session and campaign data for the sites analytics reports.  By default it is set to expire after 2 years, although this is customisable by website owners.\n",
      "\n",
      "PHPSESSID: Cookie generated by applications based on the PHP language.  This is a general purpose identifier used to maintain user session variables. It is normally a random generated number, how it is used can be specific to the site, but a good example is maintaining a logged-in status for a user between pages.\n",
      "\n",
      "__utmz: This is one of the four main cookies set by the Google Analytics service which enables website owners to track visitor behaviour measure of site performance. This cookie identifies the source of traffic to the site - so Google Analytics can tell site owners where visitors came from when arriving on the site. The cookie has a life span of 6 months and is updated every time data is sent to Google Analytics.\n",
      "\n"
     ]
    }
   ],
   "source": [
    "# display cookiepedia data\n",
    "fail_resp_msg = 'There is not yet' # begining of error message when cookiepedia has no data :(\n",
    "cache = Simple_Json_Cache(\"cookiepedia\")\n",
    "cache_data = cache.get_cache_file()\n",
    "filtered_cache = {k:v for (k,v) in cache_data.items() if v.strip() and not v.startswith(fail_resp_msg)}\n",
    "for (k,v) in filtered_cache.items():\n",
    "    print(k+\": \"+v+\"\\n\")"
   ]
  },

    "### Extract Storage Data\n",
    "\n",
    "The script initially reduces the search exclusively to function calls that contain the symbol: \"window.localStorage\"\n",
    "\n",
    "further apis to investigate: `[\"window.localStorage\", \"window.sessionStorage\", \"window.globalStorage\", \"window.Storage\"]`\n",
    "\n",
    "investigate api calls on the object, example: `window.sessionStorage.setItem(\"key\", \"val\")`. The storage APIs follow a pattern of get, set delete, etc. Could be structured into a dataframe of (key, value, function)."
   ]
